[6]intransitive stem verb
to think
[7]Thematic Relations
<strong>agent</strong> <em>subject</em>
<strong>topic</strong> <small-caps>pa</small-caps>
<strong>speech</strong> <em>dative</em>
[7]Examples
[e]<strong>&#x294;usu kuli lu&rsquo;i filli qixa pa.</strong>
[e]<small-caps>1int dat-com</small-caps> <em>love</em> <small-caps>2int pst;dyn</small-caps> <em>think.</em>
[e]&#x201c;I think I fell in love with you.&#x201d;
[f]<strong>&#x294;usu palu&rsquo;i pa.</strong>
[e]<small-caps>1int</small-caps> <em>towards-love think.</em>
[e]&#x201c;I think about love.&#x201d;
[7]Aspectual Meanings
<strong>dynamic</strong> <em>to have a thought</em>
<strong>stative</strong> <em>to be thinking</em>

[2]bitta
[3]High Lulani
[4]<high-lulani>B;t</high-lulani>
[5]/&#x2c8;bit.t&#x259;/
[6]inanimate stem noun
time
[7]Definition
the two temporal dimensions
[7]Notes
The first dimension of time is subjective: a person's birth is <em>before</em> their death.
The second dimension is objective: if one time-travels into the past, then one's death may well be <em>upstream</em> of one's birth.
[7]Derived Terms
<strong><a href="../j/janni.html">jannibitta</a></strong> <high-lulani>j;NB;t</high-lulani> <em>to time travel</em>

[2]su&rsquo;a

[4]<high-lulani>za</high-lulani>
[5]/&#x2cc;su&#x294;.&#x259;/
[6]stem pronoun
self; reflexive particle
[7]Usage Notes
replaces third-person pronouns, if necessary, to refer to the subject of the sentence. Do not take case markers. Can be used as genitive, but only as a suffix; in this case, covers both alienable and inalienable possession.
